# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all Go source files in the Kubernetes v1.32.0 repository that validate pod security context fields. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I found **12 core files** and **26 symbols** that validate pod security context fields:

### Key Files:

1. **API Validation (pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go)**: Core validation functions including `ValidateSecurityContext`, `validateSeccompProfileField`, and `validatePodSpecSecurityContext`.

2. **Pod Security Admission Policy Checks** (staging/src/k8s.io/pod-security-admission/policy/):
   - **check_privileged.go**: Validates that `privileged=true` is not set
   - **check_runAsNonRoot.go**: Enforces `runAsNonRoot=true` at pod or container level
   - **check_capabilities_baseline.go**: Restricts capabilities to a whitelist
   - **check_capabilities_restricted.go**: Requires dropping ALL capabilities
   - **check_seccompProfile_baseline.go**: Restricts seccomp profiles to safe options
   - **check_seccompProfile_restricted.go**: Requires seccomp profiles to be set
   - **check_allowPrivilegeEscalation.go**: Forbids privilege escalation

3. **Kubelet Runtime Verification**:
   - **security_context_others.go** & **security_context_windows.go**: Runtime verification of `runAsNonRoot` 
   - **helpers.go**: Seccomp profile handling

4. **Accessors (pkg/securitycontext/accessors.go)**: Safe wrapper functions for accessing security context fields

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about all files, symbols, and validation functions.

Special handling exists for user namespace pods (KEP-127).\\n\\n### Capabilities Validation\\n\\nCapabilities are validated across two checks:\\n\\n**check_capabilities_baseline.go** contains:\\n- **CheckCapabilitiesBaseline()**: A baseline-level check limiting capabilities that can be added.\\n- **capabilitiesBaseline_1_0()**: Enforces that only whitelisted capabilities (AUDIT_WRITE, CHOWN, DAC_OVERRIDE, FOWNER, FSETID, KILL, MKNOD, NET_BIND_SERVICE, SETFCAP, SETGID, SETPCAP, SETUID, SYS_CHROOT) can be added via `capabilities.Add`.\\n\\n**check_capabilities_restricted.go** contains:\\n- **CheckCapabilitiesRestricted()**: A restricted-level check requiring all capabilities to be dropped.\\n- **capabilitiesRestricted_1_22()**: Enforces that containers must include \\\"ALL\\\" in `capabilities.Drop` and can only add NET_BIND_SERVICE.\\n- **capabilitiesRestricted_1_25()**: Windows-aware version that exempts Windows pods from capability restrictions.\\n\\n### SeccompProfile **seccompProfileBaseline_1_0()**: Validates legacy seccomp annotations, restricting to runtime/default, docker/default, localhost/*, or undefined.\\n- **seccompProfileBaseline_1_19()**: Validates the newer `securityContext.seccompProfile` field, restricting to RuntimeDefault, Localhost, or undefined.\\n\\n**check_seccompProfile_restricted.go** contains:\\n- **CheckSeccompProfileRestricted()**: A restricted-level check requiring seccomp profiles to be explicitly set.\\n- **seccompProfileRestricted_1_19()**: Enforces that pods or containers must set a valid seccomp profile (RuntimeDefault or Localhost).\\n- **seccompProfileRestricted_1_25()**: Windows-aware version that exempts Windows pods from seccomp requirements.\\n\\n### AllowPrivilegeEscalation **allowPrivilegeEscalation_1_8()**: Validates that `AllowPrivilegeEscalation` is explicitly set to false on all containers.\\n- **allowPrivilegeEscalation_1_25()**: Windows-aware version that exempts container-level settings.\\n\\n## Security Context Accessors\\n\\n**pkg/securitycontext/accessors.go** provides wrapper functions for safe access to security context fields:\\n- **RunAsNonRoot()**:
